  [user_task_description] # ContentPublishingHub Web Application Specification  ## Objective Build a comprehensive content management system with version control, content scheduling, and analytics. The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.  ## Language Python (Flask framework recommended)  ## Page Design  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) **Route:** `/dashboard` **Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation **Elements:** - Page container (id: `dashboard-page`) - Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`) - Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`) - Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`) - Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/create` **Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles **Elements:** - Page container (id: `create-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`) - Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit` **Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking **Elements:** - Page container (id: `edit-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`) - Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions` **Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions **Elements:** - Page container (id: `version-history-page`) - Versions list (id: `versions-list`) - Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`) - Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`) - Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/mine` **Purpose:** List user's articles with filters **Elements:** - Page container (id: `my-articles-page`) - Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`) - Articles table (id: `articles-table`) - Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/published` **Purpose:** Public-facing content library **Elements:** - Page container (id: `published-articles-page`) - Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`) - Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`) - Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)  ### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`) **Route:** `/calendar` **Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view **Elements:** - Page container (id: `calendar-page`) - Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`) - Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`) - Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)  ### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics` **Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article **Elements:** - Page container (id: `analytics-page`) - Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`) - Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`) - Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`) - Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)  ## Data Storage  The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:  ### 1. users.txt Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ``` status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release  ### 3. article_versions.txt Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ``` status: approved, rejected, revision_requested  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```

       | content_calendar.html    | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_events` (list), POST may include scheduling result or errors |\n| `/article/<article_id>/analytics` | GET          | article_analytics         | article_analytics.html   | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict)                   |\n\n---\n\n## Section 2: HTML Template Structure\n\n### 1. dashboard.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"dashboard-page\">`\n- Welcome message: element with `id=\"welcome-message\"` to display username\n- Quick stats section: element with `id=\"quick-stats\"` to show key metrics\n- Create Article button: `<button id=\"create-article-button\">`\n- Recent activity feed: element with `id=\"recent-activity\"` to list recent actions\n\n### 2. create_article.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"create-article-page\">`\n- Article title input: `<input type=\"text\" id=\"article-title\">`\n- Content editor: `<textarea id=\"article-content\">`\n- Save as Draft button: `<button id=\"save-draft-button\">`\n- Cancel button: `<button id=\"cancel-button\">`\n\n### 3. edit_article.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"edit-article-page\">`\n- Article title input: `<input type=\"text\" id=\"edit-article-title\">`\n- Content editor: `<textarea id=\"edit-article-content\">`\n- Save New Version button: `<button id=\"save-version-button\">`\n- Cancel button: `<button id=\"cancel-edit\">`\n\n### 4. version_history.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"version-history-page\">`\n- Versions list container: `<div id=\"versions-list\">` (likely a list or table of versions)\n- Version comparison section: `<div id=\"version-comparison\">` for diff or side-by-side\n- Restore button: `<button id=\"restore-version-1\">` (Note: The \"1\" suffix is literal — ensure button ID includes version number dynamically if multiple restore buttons)\n- Back to Edit button: `<button id=\"back-to-edit-history\">`\n\n### 5. my_articles.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"my-articles-page\">`\n- Filter by status dropdown: `<select id=\"filter-article-status\">`\n- Articles table: `<table id=\"articles-table\">`\n- Create New Article button: `<button id=\"create-new-article\">`\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard\">`\n\n### 6. published_articles.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"published-articles-page\">`\n- Filter by category dropdown: `<select id=\"filter-published-category\">`\n- Articles grid container: `<div id=\"published-articles-grid\">`\n- Sort by dropdown: `<select id=\"sort-published\">`\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard-published\">`\n\n### 7. content_calendar.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"calendar-page\">`\n- Calendar view selector: `<select id=\"calendar-view\">`\n- Calendar grid container: `<div id=\"calendar-grid\">`\n- Schedule button: `<button id=\"schedule-button\">`\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard-calendar\">`\n\n### 8. article_analytics.html\n- Page container: `<div id=\"analytics-page\">`\n- Analytics overview container: `<div id=\"analytics-overview\">`\n- Total views display: element with `id=\"analytics-total-views\"`\n- Unique visitors display: element with `id=\"analytics-unique-visitors\"`\n- Back to Article button: `<button id=\"back-to-article-analytics\">`\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Data File Schemas\n\nAll data files are stored in plain text under the `data/` directory with each record on a new line and fields separated by pipe (`|`).\n\n---\n\n### 1. users.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - username (string): User's login name\n  - email (string): User's email address\n  - fullname (string): User's full name\n  - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Account creation date\n\n- Example rows:\n```\njohn|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15\nalice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16\nbob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17\nadmin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. articles.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - article_id (integer): Unique article identifier\n  - title (string): Article title\n  - author (string): Author username (matches `users.txt` username)\n  - category (string): One of [news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release]\n  - status (string): One of [draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived]\n  - tags (comma-separated string): List of tags related to the article\n  - featured_image (string): Path/URL to featured image, empty if none\n  - meta_description (string): Short meta description\n  - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Article creation date\n  - publish_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss` or empty if unpublished)\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00\n2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00\n3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. article_versions.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - version_id (integer): Unique version identifier\n  - article_id (integer): Identifier of the article this version belongs to\n  - version_number (integer): Sequential version number for this article\n  - content (string): Full article content text\n  - author (string): Username of author who made this version\n  - created_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): Timestamp of version creation\n  - change_summary (string): Text summary of changes made\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft\n2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction\n3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. approvals.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - approval_id (integer): Unique approval record identifier\n  - article_id (integer): Article identifier\n  - version_id (integer): Version identifier approved/rejected\n  - approver (string): Username who approved/rejected\n  - status (string): One of [approved, rejected, revision_requested]\n  - comments (string): Commentary left by approver\n  - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When the approval status was recorded\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00\n2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00\n3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. workflow_stages.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - stage_id (integer): Unique workflow stage identifier\n  - category (string): Article category this stage applies to\n  - stage_name (string): Name of the workflow stage (e.g., \"Editor Review\")\n  - stage_order (integer): Order of the stage in workflow\n  - is_required (string): `yes` or `no` indicating if stage is mandatory\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes\n2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes\n3|news|Editor Review|1|yes\n4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes\n5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. comments.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - comment_id (integer): Unique comment identifier\n  - article_id (integer): Article identifier this comment belongs to\n  - version_id (integer): Version identifier this comment refers to\n  - user (string): Username of commenter\n  - comment_text (string): Text content of the comment\n  - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When comment was created\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00\n2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00\n3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00\n```\n\n---\n\n### 7. analytics.txt\n- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):\n  - analytics_id (integer): Unique analytics record identifier\n  - article_id (integer): Article identifier\n  - date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Date of recorded analytics\n  - views (integer): Number of views on that date\n  - unique_visitors (integer): Count of unique visitors\n  - avg_time_seconds (integer): Average visit duration in seconds\n  - shares (integer): Number of shares on that date\n\n- Example rows:\n```\n1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12\n2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18\n3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15\n4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8\n```\n\n---\n\nThis design_spec.md document fully specifies Flask route interfaces, HTML page templates with required element IDs and structures, and the precise data file schemas with example values. Backend and frontend developers can work independently using this specification to implement the ContentPublishingHub web application."})

The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.  ## Language Python (Flask framework recommended)  ## Page Design  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) **Route:** `/dashboard` **Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation **Elements:** - Page container (id: `dashboard-page`) - Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`) - Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`) - Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`) - Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)  ### 2. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit` **Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking **Elements:** - Page container (id: `edit-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`) - Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)  ### 4.   [design_spec.md] # ContentPublishingHub Design Specification  ---  ## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification  | Route Pattern                    | HTTP Method(s) | Function Name             | Template Rendered        | Context Variables Passed to Template                     | |--------------------------------|----------------|---------------------------|--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------| | `/dashboard`                   | GET            | dashboard                 | dashboard.html           | `username` (str): Current user's username                | | `/article/create`              | GET, POST      | create_article            | create_article.html      | GET: none; POST: validation errors (dict) if any         | | `/article/<article_id>/edit`   | GET, POST      | edit_article              | edit_article.html        | `article_id` (int), `article` (dict with article data), `current_version` (dict), validation errors (POST) | | `/article/<article_id>/versions` | GET          | version_history           | version_history.html     | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `selected_version` (optional), `comparison_data` (optional) | | `/articles/mine`               | GET            | my_articles               | my_articles.html         | `username` (str), `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) | | `/articles/published`          | GET            | published_articles        | published_articles.html  | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) | | `/calendar`                   | GET, POST      | content_calendar          | content_calendar.html    | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_events` (list), POST may include scheduling result or errors | | `/article/<article_id>/analytics` | GET          | article_analytics         | article_analytics.html   | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict)                   |  ---  ## Section 2: HTML Template Structure  ### 1. dashboard.html - Page container: `<div id="dashboard-page">` - Welcome message: element with `id="welcome-message"` to display username - Quick stats section: element with `id="quick-stats"` to show key metrics - Create Article button: `<button id="create-article-button">` - Recent activity feed: element with `id="recent-activity"` to list recent actions  ### 2. create_article.html - Page container: `<div id="create-article-page">` id="cancel-button">`  ### 3. edit_article.html - Page container: `<div id="edit-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="edit-article-title">` - Content editor: `<textarea id="edit-article-content">` - Save New Version button: `<button id="save-version-button">` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">`  ### 4. version_history.html - Page container: `<div id="version-history-page">` - Versions list container: `<div id="versions-list">` (likely a list or table of versions) - Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` for diff or side-by-side - Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">` (Note: The "1" suffix is literal — ensure button ID includes version number dynamically if multiple restore buttons) - Back to Edit button: `<button id="back-to-edit-history">`  ### 5. my_articles.html - Page container: `<div id="my-articles-page">` - Filter by status dropdown: `<select id="filter-article-status">` - Articles table: `<table id="articles-table">` - Create New Article button: `<button id="create-new-article">` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard">`  ### 6. published_articles.html - id="back-to-dashboard-calendar">`  ### 8. article_analytics.html - Page container: `<div id="analytics-page">` - Analytics overview container: `<div id="analytics-overview">` - Total views display: element with `id="analytics-total-views"` - Unique visitors display: element with `id="analytics-unique-visitors"` - Back to Article button: `<button id="back-to-article-analytics">`  ---  ## Section 3: Data File Schemas  All data files are stored in plain text under the `data/` directory with each record on a new line and fields separated by pipe (`|`).  ---  ### 1. users.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - username (string): User's login name   - email (string): User's email address   - fullname (string): User's full name   - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Account creation date  - Example rows: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ---  ### 2. articles.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - article_id (integer): Unique article identifier   - title (string): Article title   - author (string): Author username (matches `users.txt` username)   - category (string): One of [news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release]   - status (string): One of [draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived]   - tags (comma-separated string): List of tags related to the article   - featured_image (string): Path/URL to featured image, empty if none   - meta_description (string): Short meta description   - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Article creation date   - publish_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss` or empty if unpublished)  - Example rows: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ```  ---  ### 3. article_versions.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - version_id (integer): Unique version identifier   - article_id (integer): Identifier of the article this version belongs to   - version_number (integer): Sequential version number for this article   - content (string): Full article content text   - author (string): Username of author who made this version   - created_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): Timestamp of version creation   - change_summary (string): Text summary of changes made  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ---  ### 4. approvals.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - approval_id (integer): Unique approval record identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier   - version_id (integer): Version identifier approved/rejected   - approver (string): Username who approved/rejected   - status (string): One of [approved, rejected, revision_requested]   - comments (string): Commentary left by approver   - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When the approval status was recorded  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ```  ---  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - stage_id (integer): Unique workflow stage identifier   - category (string): Article category this stage applies to   - stage_name (string): Name of the workflow stage (e.g., "Editor Review")   - stage_order (integer): Order of the stage in workflow   - is_required (string): `yes` or `no` indicating if stage is mandatory  - Example rows: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ---  ### 6. comments.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - comment_id (integer): Unique comment identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier this comment belongs to   - version_id (integer): Version identifier this comment refers to   - user (string): Username of commenter   - comment_text (string): Text content of the comment   - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When comment was created  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ---  ### 7. analytics.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - analytics_id (integer): Unique analytics record identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier   - date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Date of recorded analytics   - views (integer): Number of views on that date   - unique_visitors (integer): Count of unique visitors   - avg_time_seconds (integer): Average visit duration in seconds   - shares (integer): Number of shares on that date  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  This design_spec.md document fully specifies Flask route interfaces, HTML page templates with required element IDs and structures, and the precise data file schemas with example values. Backend and frontend developers can work independently using this specification to implement the ContentPublishingHub web application.

# ContentPublishingHub Web Application Specification

## Objective
Build a comprehensive content management system with version control, content scheduling, and analytics. The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.

## Language
Python (Flask framework recommended)

## Page Design

### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`)
**Route:** `/dashboard`
**Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `dashboard-page`)
- Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`)
- Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`)
- Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`)
- Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)

### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`)
**Route:** `/article/create`
**Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `create-article-page`)
- Article title input (id: `article-title`)
- Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`)
- Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`)
- Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)

### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit`
**Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `edit-article-page`)
- Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`)
- Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`)
- Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`)
- Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)

### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions`
**Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `version-history-page`)
- Versions list (id: `versions-list`)
- Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`)
- Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`)
- Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)

### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`)
**Route:** `/articles/mine`
**Purpose:** List user's articles with filters
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `my-articles-page`)
- Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`)
- Articles table (id: `articles-table`)
- Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)

### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`)
**Route:** `/articles/published`
**Purpose:** Public-facing content library
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `published-articles-page`)
- Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`)
- Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`)
- Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)

### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`)
**Route:** `/calendar`
**Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `calendar-page`)
- Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`)
- Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`)
- Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)

### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics`
**Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `analytics-page`)
- Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`)
- Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`)
- Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`)
- Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)

## Data Storage

The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:

### 1. users.txt
Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date`
Example:
```
john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15
alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16
bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17
admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10
```

### 2. articles.txt
Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date`
Example:
```
1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00
2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00
3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|
```
status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived
category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release

### 3. article_versions.txt
Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary`
Example:
```
1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft
2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction
3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version
```

### 4. approvals.txt
Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp`
Example:
```
1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00
2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00
3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00
```
status: approved, rejected, revision_requested

### 5. workflow_stages.txt
Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required`
Example:
```
1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes
2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes
3|news|Editor Review|1|yes
4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes
5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes
```

### 6. comments.txt
Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp`
Example:
```
1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00
2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00
3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00
```

### 7. analytics.txt
Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares`
Example:
```
1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12
2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18
3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15
4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8
```


=== design_spec.md ===
# ContentPublishingHub Design Specification

---

## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification

| Route Pattern                    | HTTP Method(s) | Function Name             | Template Rendered        | Context Variables Passed to Template                     |
|--------------------------------|----------------|---------------------------|--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|
| `/dashboard`                   | GET            | dashboard                 | dashboard.html           | `username` (str): Current user's username                |
| `/article/create`              | GET, POST      | create_article            | create_article.html      | GET: none; POST: validation errors (dict) if any         |
| `/article/<article_id>/edit`   | GET, POST      | edit_article              | edit_article.html        | `article_id` (int), `article` (dict with article data), `current_version` (dict), validation errors (POST) |
| `/article/<article_id>/versions` | GET          | version_history           | version_history.html     | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `selected_version` (optional), `comparison_data` (optional) |
| `/articles/mine`               | GET            | my_articles               | my_articles.html         | `username` (str), `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) |
| `/articles/published`          | GET            | published_articles        | published_articles.html  | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) |
| `/calendar`                   | GET, POST      | content_calendar          | content_calendar.html    | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_events` (list), POST may include scheduling result or errors |
| `/article/<article_id>/analytics` | GET          | article_analytics         | article_analytics.html   | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict)                   |

---

- Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">`

- Versions list container: `<div id="versions-list">` (likely a list or table of versions)
- Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` for diff or side-by-side
- Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">` (Note: The "1" suffix is literal — ensure button ID includes version number dynamically if multiple restore buttons)

## Section 3: Data File Schemas

All data files are stored in plain text under the `data/` directory with each record on a new line and fields separated by pipe (`|`).

---

### 1. users.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - username (string): User's login name
  - email (string): User's email address
  - fullname (string): User's full name
  - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Account creation date

- Example rows:
```
john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15
alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16
bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17
admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10
```

---

### 2. articles.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - article_id (integer): Unique article identifier
  - title (string): Article title
  - author (string): Author username (matches `users.txt` username)
  - category (string): One of [news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release]
  - status (string): One of [draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived]
  - tags (comma-separated string): List of tags related to the article
  - featured_image (string): Path/URL to featured image, empty if none
  - meta_description (string): Short meta description
  - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Article creation date
  - publish_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss` or empty if unpublished)

- Example rows:
```
1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00
2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00
3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|
```

---

### 3. article_versions.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - version_id (integer): Unique version identifier
  - article_id (integer): Identifier of the article this version belongs to
  - version_number (integer): Sequential version number for this article
  - content (string): Full article content text
  - author (string): Username of author who made this version
  - created_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): Timestamp of version creation
  - change_summary (string): Text summary of changes made

- Example rows:
```
1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft
2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction
3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version
```

---

### 4. approvals.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - approval_id (integer): Unique approval record identifier
  - article_id (integer): Article identifier
  - version_id (integer): Version identifier approved/rejected
  - approver (string): Username who approved/rejected
  - status (string): One of [approved, rejected, revision_requested]
  - comments (string): Commentary left by approver
  - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When the approval status was recorded

- Example rows:
```
1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00
2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00
3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00
```

---

### 5. workflow_stages.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - stage_id (integer): Unique workflow stage identifier
  - category (string): Article category this stage applies to
  - stage_name (string): Name of the workflow stage (e.g., "Editor Review")
  - stage_order (integer): Order of the stage in workflow
  - is_required (string): `yes` or `no` indicating if stage is mandatory

- Example rows:
```
1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes
2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes
3|news|Editor Review|1|yes
4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes
5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes
```

---

### 6. comments.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - comment_id (integer): Unique comment identifier
  - article_id (integer): Article identifier this comment belongs to
  - version_id (integer): Version identifier this comment refers to
  - user (string): Username of commenter
  - comment_text (string): Text content of the comment
  - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When comment was created

- Example rows:
```
1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00
2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00
3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00
```

---

### 7. analytics.txt
- Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):
  - analytics_id (integer): Unique analytics record identifier
  - article_id (integer): Article identifier
  - date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Date of recorded analytics
  - views (integer): Number of views on that date
  - unique_visitors (integer): Count of unique visitors
  - avg_time_seconds (integer): Average visit duration in seconds
  - shares (integer): Number of shares on that date

- Example rows:
```
1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12
2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18
3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15
4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8
```

Testing should start from the Dashboard page.  ## Language Python (Flask framework recommended)  ## Page Design  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) **Route:** `/dashboard` **Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation **Elements:** - Page container (id: `dashboard-page`) - Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`) - Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`) - Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`) - Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/create` **Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles **Elements:** - Page container (id: `create-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`) - Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit` **Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking **Elements:** - Page container (id: `edit-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`) - Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions` **Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions **Elements:** - Page container (id: `version-history-page`) - Versions list (id: `versions-list`) - Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`) - Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`) - Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/mine` **Purpose:** List user's articles with filters **Elements:** - Page container (id: `my-articles-page`) - Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`) - Articles table (id: `articles-table`) - Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/published` **Purpose:** Public-facing content library **Elements:** - Page container (id: `published-articles-page`) - Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`) - Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`) - Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)  ### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`) **Route:** `/calendar` **Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view **Elements:** - Page container (id: `calendar-page`) - Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`) - Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`) - Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)  ### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics` **Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article **Elements:** - Page container (id: `analytics-page`) - Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`) - Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`) - Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`) - Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)  ## Data Storage  The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:  ### 1. users.txt Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ``` status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release  ### 3. article_versions.txt Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ``` status: approved, rejected, revision_requested  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```
  [design_spec.md] # ContentPublishingHub Design Specification  ---  ## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification  | Route Pattern                    | HTTP Method(s) | Function Name             | Template Rendered        | Context Variables Passed to Template                     | |--------------------------------|----------------|---------------------------|--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------| | `/dashboard`                   | GET            | dashboard                 | dashboard.html           | `username` (str): Current user's username                | | `/article/create`              | GET, POST      | create_article            | create_article.html      | GET: none; POST: validation errors (dict) if any         | | `/article/<article_id>/edit`   | GET, POST      | edit_article              | edit_article.html        | `article_id` (int), `article` (dict with article data), `current_version` (dict), validation errors (POST) | | `/article/<article_id>/versions` | GET          | version_history           | version_history.html     | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `selected_version` (optional), `comparison_data` (optional) | | `/articles/mine`               | GET            | my_articles               | my_articles.html         | `username` (str), `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) | | `/articles/published`          | GET            | published_articles        | published_articles.html  | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) | | `/calendar`                   | GET, POST      | content_calendar          | content_calendar.html    | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_events` (list), POST may include scheduling result or errors | | `/article/<article_id>/analytics` | GET          | article_analytics         | article_analytics.html   | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict)                   |  ---  ## Section 2: HTML Template Structure  ### 1. dashboard.html - Page container: `<div id="dashboard-page">` - Welcome message: element with `id="welcome-message"` to display username - Quick stats section: element with `id="quick-stats"` to show key metrics - Create Article button: `<button id="create-article-button">` - Recent activity feed: element with `id="recent-activity"` to list recent actions  ### 2. create_article.html - Page container: `<div id="create-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="article-title">` - Content editor: `<textarea id="article-content">` - Save as Draft button: `<button id="save-draft-button">` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-button">`  ### 3. edit_article.html - Page container: `<div id="edit-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="edit-article-title">` - Content editor: `<textarea id="edit-article-content">` - Save New Version button: `<button id="save-version-button">` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">`  ### 4. version_history.html - Page container: `<div id="version-history-page">` - Versions list container: `<div id="versions-list">` (likely a list or table of versions) - Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` for diff or side-by-side - Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">` (Note: The "1" suffix is literal — ensure button ID includes version number dynamically if multiple restore buttons) - Back to Edit button: `<button id="back-to-edit-history">`  ### 5. my_articles.html - Page container: `<div id="my-articles-page">` - Filter by status dropdown: `<select id="filter-article-status">` - Articles table: `<table id="articles-table">` - Create New Article button: `<button id="create-new-article">` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard">`  ### 6. published_articles.html - Page container: `<div id="published-articles-page">` - Filter by category dropdown: `<select id="filter-published-category">` - Articles grid container: `<div id="published-articles-grid">` - Sort by dropdown: `<select id="sort-published">` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-published">`  ### 7. content_calendar.html - Page container: `<div id="calendar-page">` - Calendar view selector: `<select id="calendar-view">` - Calendar grid container: `<div id="calendar-grid">` - Schedule button: `<button id="schedule-button">` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-calendar">`  ### 8. article_analytics.html - Page container: `<div id="analytics-page">` - Analytics overview container: `<div id="analytics-overview">` - Total views display: element with `id="analytics-total-views"` - Unique visitors display: element with `id="analytics-unique-visitors"` - Back to Article button: `<button id="back-to-article-analytics">`  ---  ## Section 3: Data File Schemas  All data files are stored in plain text under the `data/` directory with each record on a new line and fields separated by pipe (`|`).  ---  ### 1. users.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - username (string): User's login name   - email (string): User's email address   - fullname (string): User's full name   - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Account creation date  - Example rows: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ---  ### 2. articles.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - article_id (integer): Unique article identifier   - title (string): Article title   - author (string): Author username (matches `users.txt` username)   - category (string): One of [news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release]   - status (string): One of [draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived]   - tags (comma-separated string): List of tags related to the article   - featured_image (string): Path/URL to featured image, empty if none   - meta_description (string): Short meta description   - created_date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Article creation date   - publish_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss` or empty if unpublished)  - Example rows: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ```  ---  ### 3. article_versions.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - version_id (integer): Unique version identifier   - article_id (integer): Identifier of the article this version belongs to   - version_number (integer): Sequential version number for this article   - content (string): Full article content text   - author (string): Username of author who made this version   - created_date (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): Timestamp of version creation   - change_summary (string): Text summary of changes made  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ---  ### 4. approvals.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - approval_id (integer): Unique approval record identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier   - version_id (integer): Version identifier approved/rejected   - approver (string): Username who approved/rejected   - status (string): One of [approved, rejected, revision_requested]   - comments (string): Commentary left by approver   - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When the approval status was recorded  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ```  ---  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - stage_id (integer): Unique workflow stage identifier   - category (string): Article category this stage applies to   - stage_name (string): Name of the workflow stage (e.g., "Editor Review")   - stage_order (integer): Order of the stage in workflow   - is_required (string): `yes` or `no` indicating if stage is mandatory  - Example rows: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ---  ### 6. comments.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - comment_id (integer): Unique comment identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier this comment belongs to   - version_id (integer): Version identifier this comment refers to   - user (string): Username of commenter   - comment_text (string): Text content of the comment   - timestamp (datetime `YYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss`): When comment was created  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ---  ### 7. analytics.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - analytics_id (integer): Unique analytics record identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier   - date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Date of recorded analytics   - views (integer): Number of views on that date   - unique_visitors (integer): Count of unique visitors   - avg_time_seconds (integer): Average visit duration in seconds   - shares (integer): Number of shares on that date  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  This design_spec.md document fully specifies Flask route interfaces, HTML page templates with required element IDs and structures, and the precise data file schemas with example values. Backend and frontend developers can work independently using this specification to implement the ContentPublishingHub web application.

rows: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ---  ### 7. analytics.txt - Fields (pipe-delimited, in order):   - analytics_id (integer): Unique analytics record identifier   - article_id (integer): Article identifier   - date (date `YYYY-MM-DD`): Date of recorded analytics   - views (integer): Number of views on that date   - unique_visitors (integer): Count of unique visitors   - avg_time_seconds (integer): Average visit duration in seconds   - shares (integer): Number of shares on that date  - Example rows: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  This design_spec.md document fully specifies Flask route interfaces, HTML page templates with required element IDs and structures, and the precise data file schemas with example values. Backend and frontend developers can work independently using this specification to implement the ContentPublishingHub web application.

draft -> under_review -> approved/rejected -> published.\n- Interaction with approval buttons and filters for visualization.\n- Scheduling managed via calendar interface with status indicators.\n\n## Authentication and User Management\n- User credentials stored in `users.txt` with email and fullname.\n- Permissions defined by role (Admin, Editor, Publisher).\n- Secure route access using session or token-based authentication.\n\n## Technologies\n- Flask for backend\n- Jinja2 for templating\n- JavaScript for frontend interactions\n- Data stored in flat files (e.g., `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `analytics.txt`)\n\n# Conclusion\nThis architecture ensures modular separation between frontend rendering and backend data management, supports rich versioning and approval workflows, and provides detailed analytics and scheduling features suitable for a content publishing platform."})

consider database migration for scalability.\n- Keep frontend modular; separate JS scripts per page.\n- Ensure error handling and user feedback mechanisms.\n"})

INPUT: === design_spec.md ===
# Design Specification for Content Publishing Hub

## Article and Versioning
- Each article identified by `article_id`.
- Multiple versions exist per article with fields: version_id, version_number, creation_date, stage (draft, review, approved, rejected), author, comments.
- Version data stored in `article_versions.txt`.
- Approval stages tracked in `approvals.txt` associated with version_id.
- Status filtering supported on frontend and backend.

## API Endpoints
- `GET /articles`: return filtered list based on status and category.
- `POST /article/create`: accepts article data and creates initial version.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: submit edits; creates new version.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: return version history.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: revert.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: returns views, visitors, average time.

## Frontend Components
- Filter inputs: Dropdowns for category, status; text inputs for search.
- Buttons to save draft, submit for approval, publish.
- Textareas for content editing identified by IDs for state management.
- Analytics page shows numeric data and charts.
- Version comparison UI for side-by-side view.

## Data structures
- Articles: title, category, content (current version), author, created_date, publish_date, tags, featured_image.
- Versions: version_number, author, create_date, stage, comment.
- Analytics: article_id, date, views, unique_visitors, avg_read_time.
- Approvals: approval_id, version_id, status (approved, rejected, under_review), approver, date.

## Workflow
- Users can create, edit, and save drafts.
- Version history accessible with restoration capability.
- Approvals require admin/editor roles.
- Analytics updated in near real-time.
- Published articles filtered and sorted via frontend controls.

## Routing
- Consistent RESTful routes with clear naming conventions.
- Frontend templates fetch data asynchronously or use server-side rendering.

## Authentication
- Login system tied to users file.
- Role-based access control to restrict actions.

## Notes
- Storage is flat-file based; consider database migration for scalability.
- Keep frontend modular; separate JS scripts per page.
- Ensure error handling and user feedback mechanisms.


=== architecture.md ===
# Content Publishing Hub Architecture

## Overview
The system is a web-based Content Publishing Hub that manages articles with version control, approvals, analytics, and scheduling. It comprises frontend and backend components developed using Flask.

## Backend Responsibilities
- Manage data storage for articles, versions, approvals, analytics, users, and workflow stages.
- Provide RESTful API endpoints for article CRUD operations, version management, approval workflow, analytics data retrieval, and scheduling.
- Handle authentication and authorization.
- Implement control flow for publishing stages: draft, review, approval, published, rejected.
- Save and retrieve article versions, manage approval status, and track analytics metrics such as views, unique visitors, and average read time.

## Frontend Responsibilities
- Render pages for article creation, editing, version comparison, analytics dashboard, calendar view, and approval workflows.
- Support form inputs for new articles, editing content, filtering and sorting articles by status, category, and stage.
- Display analytics visualizations such as total views and unique visitors per article.
- Provide controls and workflows for approvals, version restoration, and scheduling publishing.

## API Design and Routing
- `GET /articles`: List articles with filtering by status (`filter_status`), category (`filter_category`), and author.
- `POST /article/create`: Create a new article.
- `GET /article/<article_id>`: Retrieve a specific article's metadata and current version.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: Edit an article's content.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: Retrieve all versions of an article.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: Restore a previous version.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: Retrieve analytics data (views, unique visitors).
- `POST /article/<article_id>/approve`: Submit article for approval or change approval status.
- `GET /dashboard`: Retrieve user's dashboard data.
- `GET /calendar`: Retrieve publishing schedule events.

## Frontend Templates and Components
- `dashboard.html`: User dashboard overview.
- `create_article.html`: Form to create a new article.
- `edit_article.html`: Editing page with title and content fields.
- `version_history.html`: List and compare article versions.
- `article_analytics.html`: Show article performance statistics.
- `content_calendar.html`: Calendar view of scheduled articles.
- `published_articles.html`: List of published articles with filters.
- `my_articles.html`: User's articles.

## Data Flow and Integration
- Frontend sends requests with filters, article IDs, and version IDs.
- Backend responds with JSON for API calls or rendered HTML templates.
- Versioning controlled by storing metadata such as version_number, stage (draft, review, approved)
- Approval status controls rendering and workflow progression.
- Analytics data updated incrementally on article views.

## Workflow Control
- Articles move through stages: draft -> under_review -> approved/rejected -> published.
- Interaction with approval buttons and filters for visualization.
- Scheduling managed via calendar interface with status indicators.

## Authentication and User Management
- User credentials stored in `users.txt` with email and fullname.
- Permissions defined by role (Admin, Editor, Publisher).
- Secure route access using session or token-based authentication.

## Technologies
- Flask for backend
- Jinja2 for templating
- JavaScript for frontend interactions
- Data stored in flat files (e.g., `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `analytics.txt`)

# Conclusion
This architecture ensures modular separation between frontend rendering and backend data management, supports rich versioning and approval workflows, and provides detailed analytics and scheduling features suitable for a content publishing platform.

text inputs for search. - Buttons to save draft, submit for approval, publish. - Textareas for content editing identified by IDs for state management. - Analytics page shows numeric data and charts. - Version comparison UI for side-by-side view.  ## Data structures - Articles: title, category, content (current version), author, created_date, publish_date, tags, featured_image. - Versions: version_number, author, create_date, stage, comment. - Analytics: article_id, date, views, unique_visitors, avg_read_time. - Approvals: approval_id, version_id, status (approved, rejected, under_review), approver, date.  ## Workflow - Users can create, edit, and save drafts. - Version history accessible with restoration capability. - Approvals require admin/editor roles. - Analytics updated in near real-time. - Published articles filtered and sorted via frontend controls.  ## Routing - Consistent RESTful routes with clear naming conventions. - Frontend templates fetch data asynchronously or use server-side rendering.  ## Authentication - Login system tied to users file. - Role-based access control to restrict actions.  ## Notes - Storage is flat-file based; consider database migration for scalability. - Keep frontend modular; separate JS scripts per page. - Ensure error handling and user feedback mechanisms.
  [architecture.md] # Content Publishing Hub Architecture  ## Overview The system is a web-based Content Publishing Hub that manages articles with version control, approvals, analytics, and scheduling. It comprises frontend and backend components developed using Flask.  ## Backend Responsibilities - Manage data storage for articles, versions, approvals, analytics, users, and workflow stages. - Provide RESTful API endpoints for article CRUD operations, version management, approval workflow, analytics data retrieval, and scheduling. - Handle authentication and authorization. - Implement control flow for publishing stages: draft, review, approval, published, rejected. - Save and retrieve article versions, manage approval status, and track analytics metrics such as views, unique visitors, and average read time.  ## Frontend Responsibilities - Render pages for article creation, editing, version comparison, analytics dashboard, calendar view, and approval workflows. - Support form inputs for new articles, editing content, filtering and sorting articles by status, category, and stage. - Display analytics visualizations such as total views and unique visitors per article. - Provide controls and workflows for approvals, version restoration, and scheduling publishing.  ## API Design and Routing - `GET /articles`: List articles with filtering by status (`filter_status`), category (`filter_category`), and author. - `POST /article/create`: Create a new article. - `GET /article/<article_id>`: Retrieve a specific article's metadata and current version. - `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: Edit an article's content. - `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: Retrieve all versions of an article. - `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: Restore a previous version. - `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: Retrieve analytics data (views, unique visitors). - `POST /article/<article_id>/approve`: Submit article for approval or change approval status. - `GET /dashboard`: Retrieve user's dashboard data. - `GET /calendar`: Retrieve publishing schedule events.  ## Frontend Templates and Components - `dashboard.html`: User dashboard overview. - `create_article.html`: Form to create a new article. - `edit_article.html`: Editing page with title and content fields. - `version_history.html`: List and compare article versions. - `article_analytics.html`: Show article performance statistics. - `content_calendar.html`: Calendar view of scheduled articles. - `published_articles.html`: List of published articles with filters. - `my_articles.html`: User's articles.  ## Data Flow and Integration - Frontend sends requests with filters, article IDs, and version IDs. - Backend responds with JSON for API calls or rendered HTML templates. - Versioning controlled by storing metadata such as version_number, stage (draft, review, approved) - Approval status controls rendering and workflow progression. - Analytics data updated incrementally on article views.  ## Workflow Control - Articles move through stages: draft -> under_review -> approved/rejected -> published. - Interaction with approval buttons and filters for visualization. - Scheduling managed via calendar interface with status indicators.  ## Authentication and User Management - User credentials stored in `users.txt` with email and fullname. - Permissions defined by role (Admin, Editor, Publisher). - Secure route access using session or token-based authentication.  ## Technologies - Flask for backend - Jinja2 for templating - JavaScript for frontend interactions - Data stored in flat files (e.g., `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `analytics.txt`)  # Conclusion This architecture ensures modular separation between frontend rendering and backend data management, supports rich versioning and approval workflows, and provides detailed analytics and scheduling features suitable for a content publishing platform.

=== LLM_call: RequirementsAnalyst ===
INPUT: === design_spec.md ===
# Design Specification for Content Publishing Hub

## Article and Versioning
- Each article identified by `article_id`.
- Multiple versions exist per article with fields: version_id, version_number, creation_date, stage (draft, review, approved, rejected), author, comments.
- Version data stored in `article_versions.txt`.
- Approval stages tracked in `approvals.txt` associated with version_id.
- Status filtering supported on frontend and backend.

## API Endpoints
- `GET /articles`: return filtered list based on status and category.
- `POST /article/create`: accepts article data and creates initial version.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: submit edits; creates new version.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: return version history.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: revert.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: returns views, visitors, average time.

## Frontend Components
- Filter inputs: Dropdowns for category, status; text inputs for search.
- Buttons to save draft, submit for approval, publish.
- Textareas for content editing identified by IDs for state management.
- Analytics page shows numeric data and charts.
- Version comparison UI for side-by-side view.

## Data structures
- Articles: title, category, content (current version), author, created_date, publish_date, tags, featured_image.
- Versions: version_number, author, create_date, stage, comment.
- Analytics: article_id, date, views, unique_visitors, avg_read_time.
- Approvals: approval_id, version_id, status (approved, rejected, under_review), approver, date.

## Workflow
- Users can create, edit, and save drafts.
- Version history accessible with restoration capability.
- Approvals require admin/editor roles.
- Analytics updated in near real-time.
- Published articles filtered and sorted via frontend controls.

## Routing
- Consistent RESTful routes with clear naming conventions.
- Frontend templates fetch data asynchronously or use server-side rendering.

## Authentication
- Login system tied to users file.
- Role-based access control to restrict actions.

## Notes
- Storage is flat-file based; consider database migration for scalability.
- Keep frontend modular; separate JS scripts per page.
- Ensure error handling and user feedback mechanisms.


=== architecture.md ===
# Content Publishing Hub Architecture

## Overview
The system is a web-based Content Publishing Hub that manages articles with version control, approvals, analytics, and scheduling. It comprises frontend and backend components developed using Flask.

## Backend Responsibilities
- Manage data storage for articles, versions, approvals, analytics, users, and workflow stages.
- Provide RESTful API endpoints for article CRUD operations, version management, approval workflow, analytics data retrieval, and scheduling.
- Handle authentication and authorization.
- Implement control flow for publishing stages: draft, review, approval, published, rejected.
- Save and retrieve article versions, manage approval status, and track analytics metrics such as views, unique visitors, and average read time.

## Frontend Responsibilities
- Render pages for article creation, editing, version comparison, analytics dashboard, calendar view, and approval workflows.
- Support form inputs for new articles, editing content, filtering and sorting articles by status, category, and stage.
- Display analytics visualizations such as total views and unique visitors per article.
- Provide controls and workflows for approvals, version restoration, and scheduling publishing.

## API Design and Routing
- `GET /articles`: List articles with filtering by status (`filter_status`), category (`filter_category`), and author.
- `POST /article/create`: Create a new article.
- `GET /article/<article_id>`: Retrieve a specific article's metadata and current version.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: Edit an article's content.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: Retrieve all versions of an article.
- `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: Restore a previous version.
- `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: Retrieve analytics data (views, unique visitors).
- `POST /article/<article_id>/approve`: Submit article for approval or change approval status.
- `GET /dashboard`: Retrieve user's dashboard data.
- `GET /calendar`: Retrieve publishing schedule events.

## Frontend Templates and Components
- `dashboard.html`: User dashboard overview.
- `create_article.html`: Form to create a new article.
- `edit_article.html`: Editing page with title and content fields.
- `version_history.html`: List and compare article versions.
- `article_analytics.html`: Show article performance statistics.
- `content_calendar.html`: Calendar view of scheduled articles.
- `published_articles.html`: List of published articles with filters.
- `my_articles.html`: User's articles.

## Data Flow and Integration
- Frontend sends requests with filters, article IDs, and version IDs.
- Backend responds with JSON for API calls or rendered HTML templates.
- Versioning controlled by storing metadata such as version_number, stage (draft, review, approved)
- Approval status controls rendering and workflow progression.
- Analytics data updated incrementally on article views.

## Workflow Control
- Articles move through stages: draft -> under_review -> approved/rejected -> published.
- Interaction with approval buttons and filters for visualization.
- Scheduling managed via calendar interface with status indicators.

## Authentication and User Management
- User credentials stored in `users.txt` with email and fullname.
- Permissions defined by role (Admin, Editor, Publisher).
- Secure route access using session or token-based authentication.

## Technologies
- Flask for backend
- Jinja2 for templating
- JavaScript for frontend interactions
- Data stored in flat files (e.g., `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `analytics.txt`)

# Conclusion
This architecture ensures modular separation between frontend rendering and backend data management, supports rich versioning and approval workflows, and provides detailed analytics and scheduling features suitable for a content publishing platform.

[DEBUG] Review Content for FrontendDeveloper -> SystemArchitect:
  [architecture.md] # Content Publishing Hub Architecture  ## Overview The system is a web-based Content Publishing Hub that manages articles with version control, approvals, analytics, and scheduling. It comprises frontend and backend components developed using Flask.  ## Backend Responsibilities - Manage data storage for articles, versions, approvals, analytics, users, and workflow stages. - Provide RESTful API endpoints for article CRUD operations, version management, approval workflow, analytics data retrieval, and scheduling. - Handle authentication and authorization. - Implement control flow for publishing stages: draft, review, approval, published, rejected. - Save and retrieve article versions, manage approval status, and track analytics metrics such as views, unique visitors, and average read time.  ## Frontend Responsibilities - Render pages for article creation, editing, version comparison, analytics dashboard, calendar view, and approval workflows. - Support form inputs for new articles, editing content, filtering and sorting articles by status, category, and stage. - Display analytics visualizations such as total views and unique visitors per article. - Provide controls and workflows for approvals, version restoration, and scheduling publishing.  ## API Design and Routing - `GET /articles`: List articles with filtering by status (`filter_status`), category (`filter_category`), and author. - `POST /article/create`: Create a new article. - `GET /article/<article_id>`: Retrieve a specific article's metadata and current version. - `POST /article/<article_id>/edit`: Edit an article's content. - `GET /article/<article_id>/versions`: Retrieve all versions of an article. - `POST /article/<article_id>/version/<version_id>/restore`: Restore a previous version. - `GET /article/<article_id>/analytics`: Retrieve analytics data (views, unique visitors). - `POST /article/<article_id>/approve`: Submit article for approval or change approval status. - `GET /dashboard`: Retrieve user's dashboard data. - `GET /calendar`: Retrieve publishing schedule events.  ## Frontend Templates and Components - `dashboard.html`: User dashboard overview. - `create_article.html`: Form to create a new article. - `edit_article.html`: Editing page with title and content fields. - `version_history.html`: List and compare article versions. - `article_analytics.html`: Show article performance statistics. - `content_calendar.html`: Calendar view of scheduled articles. - `published_articles.html`: List of published articles with filters. - `my_articles.html`: User's articles.  ## Data Flow and Integration - Frontend sends requests with filters, article IDs, and version IDs. - Backend responds with JSON for API calls or rendered HTML templates. - Versioning controlled by storing metadata such as version_number, stage (draft, review, approved) - Approval status controls rendering and workflow progression. - Analytics data updated incrementally on article views.  ## Workflow Control - Articles move through stages: draft -> under_review -> approved/rejected -> published. - Interaction with approval buttons and filters for visualization. - Scheduling managed via calendar interface with status indicators.  ## Authentication and User Management - User credentials stored in `users.txt` with email and fullname. - Permissions defined by role (Admin, Editor, Publisher). - Secure route access using session or token-based authentication.  ## Technologies - Flask for backend - Jinja2 for templating - JavaScript for frontend interactions - Data stored in flat files (e.g., `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `analytics.txt`)  # Conclusion This architecture ensures modular separation between frontend rendering and backend data management, supports rich versioning and approval workflows, and provides detailed analytics and scheduling features suitable for a content publishing platform.
